<div id="review_1913303044" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1913303044" />
    <a title="Ana " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5237420-ana"><img alt="Ana " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573472177p2/5237420.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1913303044?book_show_action=true">Feb 17, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ana " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ana " href="/user/show/5237420-ana">Ana </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780141039954" href="/book/show/6650039-notes-on-a-scandal">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5237420-ana?shelf=of-self">of-self</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5237420-ana?shelf=fallen-characters">fallen-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5237420-ana?shelf=love-me-again">love-me-again</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5237420-ana?shelf=brainy-psychological">brainy-psychological</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5237420-ana?shelf=page-turner">page-turner</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5237420-ana?shelf=absolute">absolute</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5237420-ana?shelf=sex-drugs-rocknroll">sex-drugs-rocknroll</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1913303044" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12583687010166981494">Spoilers everywhere. <br/><br/>This book starts where you expect and ends where you have no idea what just happened. A truly gripping ride. <br/><br/>The three characters of this book that stand out: Barbara (60, history teacher), Sheba(40, pottery teacher) and Connoly (15, their student). While the story is told in Barbara's diary, the scandal of which the title speaks is the sexual relationship between Sheba and Connolly, her pupil. You might start the book with the knowledge that you are appalled by such an idea</span>
  <span id="freeText12583687010166981494" style="display:none">Spoilers everywhere. <br /><br />This book starts where you expect and ends where you have no idea what just happened. A truly gripping ride. <br /><br />The three characters of this book that stand out: Barbara (60, history teacher), Sheba(40, pottery teacher) and Connoly (15, their student). While the story is told in Barbara's diary, the scandal of which the title speaks is the sexual relationship between Sheba and Connolly, her pupil. You might start the book with the knowledge that you are appalled by such an idea, but trust me, this is not your typical I'm-your-teacher-and-I'm-a-pervert type of story. <br /><br />Now, really, spoilers everywhere. <br /><br />Barbara is fucking evil. Not only is she a virgin 60 year old that has a vicious tongue, but she also makes Sheba become dependent on her in a very manipulative and subtle way, so much so that you get hints throughout the book, but by the end it's like Barbara took off her circus mask in the finale of her act only to reveal an even uglier face underneath. She is the one that turns Sheba in, out of spite and viciousness that you can only guess under the pretense of an old teacher. She is so lonely that she wants to be important for someone, so important that she becomes the sole carer of them, so caring that she becomes their only life-line. She picks Sheba not because they were predestined to be together, but because Sheba is ... well ... spineless. <br /><br />Sheba is indeed a malleable character. She morphs into whatever shape you give her. She married at 20 with her 20-years-older-than-her lecturer because she never thought she could take care of herself. She has two children, Polly the teenager who wears t-shirts with "Bitch Goddess" imprinted on them and Ben, a little boy with Down syndrome. She secretly finds no happiness in this, but she accepts her form as it is given to her by her role as caring wife and mother of a disabled child. When Connolly comes around and compliments her on her looks - like only a fifteen year old in which hormones are gathered up at the tip of his penis and are yelling in unison can do - she falls for it. You might say she puts up a fight. That was not a fight, if I've ever seen one. She complacently has sex with him, after he becomes a bit of a stalker and tries to forcefully kiss her, and then falls madly in love with him. <br /><br />Connolly... I mean, what can I say? Teenager boy who wants to fuck his hot teacher. Have we never heard this story before? I was fifteen once. If any female teacher who managed to look even remotely hot presided over my class, my friends' eyes would have a glazed look, as if they're there, but not totally there. Probably thinking about fucking her over her desk - which, by the way, is more of a way of sexualizing power than of sexualizing the actual woman; it comes down to how a pupil would embrace the role of having his teacher, who holds power over him, to become submissive to his own desire, and that a fifteen year old would only understand as the result of having sex. Nothing surprising there. <br /><br />What was surprising and lovely to read, though, was Barbara's slow ascent to power. Power over the situation, power over Sheba. This book is absolutely great in terms of character building and, even though I found myself angry at this wretched woman, I can also step back and admire the craftsmanship in penning her to her last old, withered, gray hair. <br /><br />Read it! </span>
  <a data-text-id="12583687010166981494" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1663764416" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1663764416" />
    <a title="Em*bedded-in-books*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2481560-em-bedded-in-books"><img alt="Em*bedded-in-books*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605433673p2/2481560.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1663764416?book_show_action=true">Oct 20, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Em*bedded-in-books*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Em*bedded-in-books*" href="/user/show/2481560-em-bedded-in-books">Em*bedded-in-books*</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">poeple who like dark and unconventional tales with antiheroes</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2481560-em-bedded-in-books?shelf=buddy-group-reads">buddy-group-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2481560-em-bedded-in-books?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2481560-em-bedded-in-books?shelf=awards">awards</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1663764416" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3376003604726166875">A harrowing read..a taboo subject.. and human lives and emotions caught up in tangles.<br/>Bathsheba, the 42 year old Pottery teacher is being pursued by law for having 'seduced' her 16 year old male student. The story unfolds through the eyes of Barbara, a senior teacher of the same school as where Sheba teaches, and who has slowly but surely become an indispensable friend to Sheba. Barbara is the only pillar of support for Sheba during her difficult circumstances.<br/>When the events unfolded, Sheba was</span>
  <span id="freeText3376003604726166875" style="display:none">A harrowing read..a taboo subject.. and human lives and emotions caught up in tangles.<br />Bathsheba, the 42 year old Pottery teacher is being pursued by law for having 'seduced' her 16 year old male student. The story unfolds through the eyes of Barbara, a senior teacher of the same school as where Sheba teaches, and who has slowly but surely become an indispensable friend to Sheba. Barbara is the only pillar of support for Sheba during her difficult circumstances.<br />When the events unfolded, Sheba was a complacently married lady with 2 children, a troublesome daughter of 17 and a younger more malleable son who had Down's syndrome. Her husband Richard, comfortably settled in life is much older than her. <br />The boy, Steven Connelly seems to be a normal lower middle class teen with crude behavior, who was attracted to Sheba's beauty, as many others, but who was courageous enough to pursue her and gain her attention.<br />Sheba did behave very irresponsibly in encouraging his advances, after a cursory refusal, and then headlong falling into a torrid physical affair, and later becoming emotionally dependent on the boy, and considering him her beau. <br />The boy Steven is nothing to be proud of, and however much I try to fathom what made Sheba fall for him, other than the only fact that I can think of (his pursuing her made her feel deliciously wanted and attractive) I never can come at a satisfactory conclusion. <br />Slowly people around start becoming suspicious, and they are exposed. Connelly, being younger and officially not yet an adult, escapes persecution, whereas Sheba loses her comfortable life and stature, and becomes totally dependent on Barbara for her survival.<br />Barbara, through her monologue, slowly exposes her true nature... and me, the reader was shocked, though I sort of guessed at where all this was leading to. <br />All characters here were sketched with precise and unforgiving sharp lines, and all the foibles of human nature were exposed. <br />I sequentially pitied, empathied and abhorred the characters in this dismal human drama.<br />The book left me with a wringing sensation, a dull, deep headache and overall gloom.<br />It is such a gloomy tale told with such a grim voice.<br />I wonder what will be Sheba's future. <br />Shall watch the movie for sure, just to grasp the faint nuances that I per chance missed while reading the book. <br /><br />Let me end by saying the title is apt- "WHAT WAS SHE THNKING? !!!"</span>
  <a data-text-id="3376003604726166875" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('jrj3hGiGMh8THMpfrj1TcPu4S1f3US+m8ue8uK+HtcT9LRAKrr+MViMLZ3l/ELmsa6p4+9bNj7rvdrRlukr6Hw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('bFX4BXXFW9PCY691/N/pK8GEWpNqBFXADzopmAkx6zsfwB+Ls/zlmvJ0AlMt8gP3UZZpP0uY9dwSqyFFHPyk4A==')})
  }

Saved from death in California\'s Monument Valley by none other than Henry Fo<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText3274744832579190128\" style=\"display:none\">The triumphant conclusion to the trilogy that began with &quot;A Star Called Henry&quot;  Roddy Doyle\'s irrepressible Irish rebel Henry Smart is back-and he is not mellowing with age. Saved from death in California\'s Monument Valley by none other than Henry Fonda, he ends up in Hollywood collaborating with legendary director John Ford on a script based on his life. Returning to Ireland in 1951 to film &quot;The Quiet Man&quot;- which to Henry\'s consternation has been completely sentimentalized-he severs his relationship with Ford.  His career in film over, Henry settles into a quiet life in a village north of Dublin, where he finds work as a caretaker for a boys\' school and takes up with a woman named Missus O\'Kelly, whom he suspects- but is not quite sure-may be his long-lost wife, the legendary Miss O\'Shea. After being injured in a political bombing in Dublin in 1974, Henry is profiled in the newspaper and suddenly the secret of his rebel past is out. Henry is a national hero. Or are his troubles just beginning?  Raucous, colorful, epic, and full of intrigue and incident, &quot;The Dead Republic&quot; is also a moving love story-the magnificent final act in the life of one of Roddy Doyle\'s most unforgettable Schnurmacher\'s voice resonates with a lyrical cadence all his own and an unsettling candor reminiscent of humorist David Sedaris and essayist Augusten Burroughs. Sparkling with chutzpah and charm, this is a story of a family\'s cultural collision and delightful dysfunction. They figured out early on that conventional values were not enough. It was their moxie that allowed them to succeed Schmooze with the passing parade that includes John Lennon, Elizabeth Taylor and Crystal Nacht. You will laugh out loud as you meet a cast of supporting characters who redefine eccentric: the 50-minute therapist, the psychic rabbi and a superstitious hypochondriac named Paris. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer16031256999060074882">Zoe Heller was born in London in 1965 and educated at Oxford University and Columbia University, New York. She is a journalist who, after writing book reviews for various newspapers, became a feature writer for The Independent. She wrote a weekly confessional column for the Sunday Times for four years, but now writes for the Daily Telegraph and earned the title 'Columnist of the Year' in 2002. <br/><br/>She</span>
  <span id="freeText16031256999060074882" style="display:none">Zoe Heller was born in London in 1965 and educated at Oxford University and Columbia University, New York. She is a journalist who, after writing book reviews for various newspapers, became a feature writer for The Independent. She wrote a weekly confessional column for the Sunday Times for four years, but now writes for the Daily Telegraph and earned the title 'Columnist of the Year' in 2002. <br /><br />She is the author of three novels: Everything You Know (2000), a dark comedy about misanthropic writer Willy Miller, Notes on a Scandal (2003) which tells the story of an affair between a high school teacher and her student through the eyes of the teacher's supposed friend, Barbara Covett and her latest - The Believers (2008). <br /><br />Zoe Heller lives in New York. </span>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/18650-notes-on-a-scandal">Quotes from What Was She Thin...</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Being alone is <i>not</i> the most awful thing in the world. You visit your museums and cultivate your interests and remind yourself how lucky you are not to be one of those spindly Sudanese children with flies beading their mouths. You make out To Do lists - reorganise linen cupboard, learn two sonnets. You dole out little treats to yourself - slices of ice-cream cake, concerts at Wigmore Hall. And then, every once in a while, you wake up and gaze out of the window at another bloody daybreak, and think, <i>I cannot do this anymore. I cannot pull myself together again and spend the next fifteen hours of wakefulness fending off the fact of my own misery</i>.<br /><br />People like Sheba think that they know what it's like to be lonely. They cast their minds back to the time they broke up with a boyfriend in 1975 and endured a whole month before meeting someone new. Or the week they spent in a Bavarian steel town when they were fifteen years old, visiting their greasy-haired German pen pal and discovering that her hand-writing was the best thing about her. But about the drip drip of long-haul, no-end-in-sight solitude, they know nothing. They don't know what it is to construct an entire weekend around a visit to the laundrette. Or to sit in a darkened flat on Halloween night, because you can't bear to expose your bleak evening to a crowd of jeering trick-or-treaters. Or to have the librarian smile pityingly and say, âGoodness, you're a quick reader!â when you bring back seven books, read from cover to cover, a week after taking them out. They don't know what it is to be so chronically untouched that the accidental brush of a bus conductor's hand on your shoulder sends a jolt of longing straight to your groin. I have sat on park benches and trains and schoolroom chairs, feeling the great store of unused, objectless love sitting in my belly like a stone until I was sure I would cry out and fall, flailing, to the ground. About all of this, Sheba and her like have no clue.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/167493-being-alone-is-not-the-most-awful-thing-in-the">214 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;There are certain people in whom you can detect the seeds of madness - seeds that have remained dormant only because the people in question have lived relatively comfortable, middle class lives. They function perfectly well in the world, but you can imagine, given a nasty parent, or a prolonged bout of unemployment, how their potential for craziness might have been realized.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/38664-there-are-certain-people-in-whom-you-can-detect-the">113 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
        <a class="actionLink" style="float: right" href="/work/quotes/18650-notes-on-a-scandal">More quotes&hellip;</a>
